# Puntovivo Roadmap

> Updated: May 18, 2026
> Single source of truth for project status, priorities, and actionable work plan.
> Replaces: `IMPLEMENTATION_STATUS.md`, `OPEN_BACKLOG.md`, `MIGRATION_PLAN.md`
> Strategic reference: see [PLAN.md](./PLAN.md) for competitive analysis, academic frameworks, and detailed technical designs.
> Sellability reference: see [SELLABILITY.md](./SELLABILITY.md) for the Colombian retail go/no-go checklist.
> Architecture diagram: [architecture.svg](./architecture.svg) (source: [architecture.mmd](./architecture.mmd))

---

## 0. MVP Colombia — Definition of Done

Concrete go/no-go checklist for declaring Puntovivo **ready to be sold to a
Colombian retail business**. Derived from the April 2026 audit of features,
DIAN regulation (Resolución 000165/2023), and hardware expectations of
neighborhood retail.

| # | Capability | Status | Blocking phase |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | Multi-tenant POS with cash sessions, sales, returns, voids, split payments, quotations | **Shipped** | Phase 0-5 done |
| 2 | Site-owned inventory + atomic transfers with discrepancy reporting | **Shipped** | Phase 2 done |
| 3 | Audit trail on sensitive actions (void, refund, cash close, stock adjust) | **Shipped** | Tier-2 #8 done |
| 4 | **Electronic invoicing (DEE + Factura Electrónica) via DIAN-authorized PT** | **Gated** — domain/model shipped, real PT pending | Phase 11 (was deferred, now **P0**) |
| 5 | **CUFE/CUDE generation + QR on printed receipt + XML ≥5-year retention** | **Partial** — CUFE/model/XML surfaces exist; final QR/retention proof pending | Phase 11 |
| 6 | **Contingency mode** (offline → queued → sent when online) for fiscal docs | **Partial** — status/UI scaffold exists; retry daemon pending | Phase 11 |
| 7 | **Barcode scanner support** (USB HID keyboard-wedge + EAN-13 checksum) | **Not started** | Phase 12 Hardware |
| 8 | **ESC/POS thermal printer driver + cash drawer opening via RJ11** | **Not started** | Phase 12 Hardware |
| 9 | **Payment terminal integration** (manual capture exists; Bold/Wompi adapter needed) | **Partial (manual only)** | Phase 12 Hardware |
| 10 | **Park-and-resume multiple carts** (suspended sales workspace) | **Shipped** | `ENG-018`, `ENG-018b`, `ENG-018c` |

**Overall MVP Colombia retail readiness: ~76% by shipped foundation,
but not sellable yet**. DIAN PT, fiscal contingency, ESC/POS + drawer,
scanner, and payment-terminal policy remain the go/no-go blockers. See
[SELLABILITY.md](./SELLABILITY.md) for the pilot / production checklist,
and section "Market Segments Coverage" below for the three-ring definition
(retail → restaurant/pharmacy → services).

---

## 1. Current State — What's Done

The application is past early migration. The core POS surface is live and operational.

### Completed Phases

| Phase | Scope | Status |
| --- | --- | --- |
| Phase 0 | Foundation, schema, transport baseline | **Complete** |
| Phase 1 | Administration and master catalogs | **Complete** |
| Phase 2 | Product management and pricing | **Complete** |
| Phase 3 | Inventory | **Complete** |
| Phase 4 | Sales / POS | **Complete** |
| Phase 5 | Procurement | **Complete** |
| Phase 6 | Reporting, sync, desktop ops, UX polish | **Advanced** |

### Implemented Surface

**Backend tRPC routers** (31 routers): health, auth, companies, countries, identificationTypes, personTypes, regimeTypes, clientTypes, commercialActivities, dashboard, departments, cities, logos, providers, sequentials, units, vatRates, categories, products, orders, customers, purchases, sales, **cashSessions** (Phase 1), inventory, locations, sites, sync, **transfers** (Phase 2), **quotations** (Phase 5), **auditLogs** (Phase 8 / Tier-2 #8), users. For the authoritative list, see [packages/server/src/trpc/router.ts](../packages/server/src/trpc/router.ts).

**Web route modules**: Dashboard, Company, Sites, Sequentials, Locations, Customer Catalogs, Geography, Providers, Categories, Units, VAT Rates, Products, Orders, Purchases, Customers, Sales, Cash Sessions, Inventory, Transfers, Quotations, Audit Logs, Users

**Desktop features**: embedded backend lifecycle, receipt printing, backup/restore, tray/theme/update settings, sync status and trigger APIs, offline DB bridge

### Unique Differentiators

- True offline-first with local SQLite
- Desktop-native Electron (no competitor offers this)
- Open source, no subscription fees, self-hosted
- Colombian/LatAm focus
- tRPC-first transport with type safety end-to-end

---

## 2. What to Build Next — Priority Order

This is the recommended implementation sequence. Each item links to its detailed phase below.

### Tier 1: Deployment Blockers (must ship before pilots)

| # | Item | Why | Phase |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1 | **i18n foundation** (es-CO/es/en) | English-only UI blocks LatAm deployment. Every new feature adds more hardcoded strings. | Pre-Phase 1 — **Shipped** |
| 2 | **Integer → real migration** for stock/quantity | Blocks ferreterías (2.5m cable) and supermarkets (0.75kg produce). #1 schema blocker. | Phase 1 — **Shipped** |
| 3 | **Cash management and shift control** | Every competitor has this. No cash session = no accountability = no LatAm retail adoption. | Phase 1 — **Shipped** |
| **3a** | **Colombia DIAN fiscal compliance** (DEE + Factura Electrónica via Proveedor Tecnológico) | **Legal blocker since May/July 2024.** Selling Puntovivo to a CO business without this creates fiscal exposure for the user and brand damage for us. See [FISCAL-INTEGRATION.md](./FISCAL-INTEGRATION.md) and [RECEIPT-TEMPLATES.md](./RECEIPT-TEMPLATES.md) (QR + CUFE on the print representation). | **Phase 11 → now P0** |
| **3b** | **POS hardware basics** (ESC/POS printer, cash drawer, barcode scanner) | Operational blocker — real stores need a physical receipt with cut, a drawer that opens, and scan-to-add. See [HARDWARE-POS.md](./HARDWARE-POS.md). | **Phase 12 → now P0** |
| **3c** | **POS touch UI + multi-surface routes** | Retail stores with all-in-one touch terminals and restaurants with KDS / customer display / mobile waiter need variant UI over the same bundle. See [UI-SURFACES.md](./UI-SURFACES.md) and [RECEIPT-TEMPLATES.md](./RECEIPT-TEMPLATES.md) for the print-layout editor that ships alongside. | **Phase 6c → P1** |

### Tier 2: Core Commercial Gaps (competitive table stakes)

| # | Item | Why | Phase |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 4 | Site-owned inventory + transfers | Stock must belong to a site, not the tenant. Transfer workflows need in-transit state. | Phase 2 |
| 5 | Split payments / multi-tender | Basic expectation: pay partially with cash and card. Foundation **shipped** (`sale_payments` table, split-aware `sales.create`, split-tender UI, cash-method-only cash-session accounting). Credit-mix is deferred to Phase 5 alongside on-account sales and abonos. | Phase 5 |
| 6 | Quotations / estimates | B2B, ferreterías, service businesses all need pre-sale conversion. **MVP shipped**: `quotations` + `quotation_items` tables, `quotations.create/list/getById/updateStatus/delete` tRPC, dedicated Quotations page with status badges and draft-only delete, Blob-URL printable receipt + Electron bridge, CSV/Excel/PDF history export, and the `accepted → converted` terminal close that lets an operator mark a quote as resolved once the corresponding sale has been completed through the regular POS. Version history, margin analysis, follow-up reminders, and an auto-prefill sale flow are deferred to later steps. | Phase 5 |
| 7 | Credit sales (ventas a crédito) | Deeply embedded LatAm practice — installments, abonos, contractor accounts. | Phase 5 Ext |
| 8 | Audit trail for sensitive actions | Required for operational trust — void, refund, price override, user change. Foundation **shipped**: `audit_logs` table + transactional `writeAuditLog` helper; admin-only `auditLogs.list` tRPC with filters (action / resourceType / resourceId / actor / date range); `/audit-logs` admin page with filter bar, translated action badges, per-action summary, CSV/Excel/PDF export. **Sensitive-action coverage expanded**: `sales.void`, `sales.returnSale` (refund), `cashSessions.close` (captures over/short), and `inventory.adjustStock` (no-op delta skipped) now emit audit rows alongside the existing `transfers.void`, `quotations.delete`, `quotations.updateStatus` (convert only). `AuditSummary` renders a per-action human string for every audited surface. Remaining gaps: price override, `purchases.void`, `user.disable` — addable by calling `writeAuditLog` from those services with no schema migration. | Phase 8 |

### Tier 3: Market Differentiation

| # | Item | Why | Phase |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 9 | Outbound logistics (pick/pack/ship) | Needed for any store with delivery. | Phase 3 |
| 10 | Promotions / loyalty / gift cards | Behind mainstream POS expectations. | Phase 7 |
| 11 | Colombia DIAN fiscal compliance | DEE + factura electrónica mandatory. Siigo/Alegra own this today. | Phase 11 |
| 12 | Country-parametrizable fiscal rules | Current Colombia-hardcoded logic blocks any non-CO deployment. | Phase 11 Ext |

### Tier 4: Vertical Expansion (after platform is solid)

| # | Item | Phase |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 13 | Multi-vertical module activation system | Phase 0 Foundation |
| 14 | Product variants, serial/lot/batch/expiry | Phase 6 |
| 15 | Restaurant module (tables, KDS, modifiers, tips) | Phase 12 |
| 16 | Pharmacy module (Rx, controlled substances, INVIMA) | Phase 13 |
| 17 | Supermarket module (scales, PLU, perishables) | Phase 14 |
| 18 | Ferretería module (unit conversion, project quoting) | Phase 15 |

### Tier 5: Platform Maturity

| # | Item | Phase |
| --- | --- | --- |
| 19 | Advanced reporting / BI (GMROI, ABC, CLV) | Phase 9 |
| 20 | Hybrid SQLite + PostgreSQL data topology | Phase 10 |
| 21 | Public API, webhooks, integration ecosystem | Phase 11 |
| 22 | Employee shifts, commissions, time tracking | Phase 8 |
| 23 | Transport execution (dispatch, tracking, POD) | Phase 4 |

### Market Segments Coverage — Three Rings

Puntovivo's market strategy is organized into three concentric rings. Each
ring activates via the **module activation system** (see [MODULE-ACTIVATION.md](./MODULE-ACTIVATION.md))
so a minimarket does not carry restaurant or pharmacy code at runtime.

**Ring 1 — Generic retail MVP (target: 8-10 weeks)**
- Neighborhood store, minimarket, papelería, ferretería, boutique with
  variants, carnicería/fruver with scale integration, panadería, heladería.
- Prerequisites: Tier-1 items 3a (DIAN fiscal) + 3b (hardware) + product
  variants + scale.
- Coverage goal: ~80% of Colombian retail POS market.

**Ring 2 — Restaurant + Pharmacy (target: +8-10 weeks after Ring 1)**
- Restaurant: composition/BOM + preparation lifecycle (KDS + tables +
  modifiers) + touch UI + one delivery integration (Rappi). See
  [RESTAURANT-LIFECYCLE.md](./RESTAURANT-LIFECYCLE.md) and
  [PRODUCT-COMPOSITION.md](./PRODUCT-COMPOSITION.md).
- Pharmacy/droguería: batches + expiration (Phase 7) + INVIMA code
  validation + prescription workflow.
- Coverage goal: ~35% additional market (gastronomy + pharma chains).

**Ring 3 — Service verticals (target: +12 weeks after Ring 2)**
- Salons, barbers, spas, vet clinics, workshops: shared appointments
  module + services-as-products + commissions + client assets.
- Optional extensions: gyms (subscriptions), laundromats (tickets),
  motels (rooms).

**Beyond Ring 3**: future verticals (CO + LatAm), LatAm country fiscal
expansion, cross-cutting platform features (BI, franchises, public API,
AI). See [FUTURE-VERTICALS.md](./FUTURE-VERTICALS.md),
[LATAM-EXPANSION.md](./LATAM-EXPANSION.md), and
[LONG-TERM-VISION.md](./LONG-TERM-VISION.md).

---

## 3. Open Technical Risks

### Platform Foundation

- **Fiscal rules are Colombia-hardcoded** — IVA rates, INC, propina (Ley 1935/2018), DIAN endpoints, fiscal regime codes are constants. Must become profile-driven before non-CO deployment. (Phase 11 Ext)
- **No module activation system** — prerequisite for multi-vertical support. (Phase 0)
- **Credit sales (ventas a crédito) missing** — no installment schedules, no abono posting, no configurable credit settings per tenant/company/site. (Phase 5 Ext)
- **Schema changes now flow through versioned Drizzle migrations** after `ENG-002`. `runSchemaSync()` and the raw-DDL mirror in `packages/server/src/db/index.ts` are retired; new schema work edits `schema.ts`, generates a migration, and updates the Drizzle journal. Remaining risk: non-additive migrations still need careful hand-written transition scripts and upgrade testing for existing SQLite installs. (Follow-up: `TEST-002`)

### Sync and Offline

- No formal hybrid data topology contract for local SQLite + remote authority. (Phase 10)
- Persistence is tightly coupled to SQLite-specific Drizzle and `better-sqlite3`. Repository interfaces are not yet extracted from router procedures. (Ticket `API-001` / `ENG-010`)
- Remote replication story is underspecified. (Phase 10)
- Structured logging is now in place across `packages/server` and the Electron main process, but request tracing / correlation IDs are still missing. (Follow-up to `ENG-006`)

### Security

- ~~Main `BrowserWindow` still runs with `sandbox: false`~~ — **shipped as ENG-004** (see Tier-6 table below). The main window now runs under `sandbox: true` with `contextIsolation: true` and `nodeIntegration: false`; the invariant is pinned by `apps/desktop/src/main/__tests__/window-config.test.ts` and enforced in `ci:desktop`.
- ~~`writeAuditLog` wired into only three operations~~ — **fully shipped as ENG-007** (2026-05-19). `writeAuditLog` fires transactionally from `transfers.void`, `quotations.delete`, `quotations.updateStatus` (convert only), `sales.void`, `sales.returnSale`, `sales.price_override`, `sales.complete`, `cashSessions.close`, `inventory.adjustStock`, `purchases.void`, `users.create`, `users.update` (role/isActive changes), `customers.update` (creditLimit changes only), and `completeSale` (when admin credit-override actually rescues an exceeded cupo). The original `company_credit_settings` gap was closed by auditing the two real mutation surfaces that ENG-090 chose instead of creating that table — see the §3b ENG-007 Shipped summary for the design rationale.
- ~~Rate limiting only global~~ — **shipped as ENG-008 + ENG-008b**. `auth.login` has dedicated rate limits (10/IP/60s, 5-failure/username/15min) with `AUTH_RATE_LIMIT_EXCEEDED` error codes and 14 tests from ENG-008; ENG-008b promoted the counters to a DB-backed `login_attempts` table with the in-memory Maps demoted to a write-through cache so a server restart no longer wipes the buckets mid-attack.

### Testing

- `apps/desktop` has a single automated test today (`src/main/__tests__/window-config.test.ts` pinning the sandbox invariant from ENG-004). Broader desktop unit coverage is still pending; most verification is manual.
- A cross-surface E2E suite against the renderer + embedded backend + Electron bridge is partially shipped. The web Playwright suite (`npm run test:e2e:web`) now covers login, role gating, every sidebar module, Spanish localisation, responsive shell, quotations, split-payment sale details, the full transactional lifecycle for sales (complete / refund / void), purchases (complete / return / void), stock adjustments, inter-site transfers (with and without discrepancy, plus the over-receipt client-side block), opening a cash session from zero, manual paid-in cash movements, and cash-session closures (overage, shortage, balanced). 25 tests run in parallel locally and the web suite runs in CI; the local-only Electron smoke (`npm run test:e2e:electron`) covers embedded-server boot, login, dashboard, and the zero-client-issue invariant. Remaining gap: Electron-in-CI. (Ticket `ENG-001`)
- Coverage thresholds are enforced in `ci:web` and `ci:server` via `vitest --coverage --run`. Web thresholds are now `70/70/70/70` after ENG-003b shipped the 13 new + 6 extended test files closing every axis. (Tickets `ENG-003`, `ENG-003b`)

### Build / CI

- Desktop packaging for `.dmg` (macOS) and `.exe` (Windows) is still exercised exclusively via the manual `release.yml` workflow. `ENG-005` now covers `ci:desktop` on Linux/macOS/Windows, but packaging/signing regressions can still hide until release time. (Ticket `ENG-005`)
- No dependency audit (`npm audit` / Dependabot alerts) gate is wired into CI. (Ticket `ENG-009`)

### Frontend Health

- Several feature components exceed 900 lines (`ProductFormModal.tsx`, `InventoryPage.tsx`, `SalesPage.tsx`) and mix data-fetch, state, and presentation. Candidates for extraction of subcomponents + custom hooks. (Ticket `ENG-011`)
- ~~`zustand` is declared in `apps/web/package.json` but has **zero imports** in `apps/web/src/`~~ — **adopted via ENG-018b's `useCartWorkspaceStore`**. Zustand is now a live, tested dependency backing the multi-cart sales workspace (ENG-012 is Shipped). Migrating the remaining Context providers (`AuthProvider`, `TenantProvider`) stays available as a future refactor if ever desired.

### Performance and UX

- Responsive/mobile refinement is weaker in admin/maintenance screens.
- Not every screen uses the same feedback quality level yet.

---

## 3b. Engineering Quality Backlog — Cross-Cutting

These tickets don't belong to any single vertical or commercial phase. They protect the app's long-term maintainability and scalability, and should be sequenced against Tier 1–3 work rather than deferred to "someday". Each ticket is actionable in isolation and has a clear acceptance test.

**Status values** (machine-readable pool discovery):

- `Pending` — never started; eligible for next sprint.
- `Partial` — some sub-steps shipped, remainder listed at the end of the Scope cell under "Remaining:". Still eligible; the agent executes the remaining items as the ticket scope.
- `Shipped` — closed; Scope cell ends with a "Shipped: …" summary. Excluded from pool.
- `Gated` — external dependency (hardware, contract, credentials) blocks start. The gate is documented inside Scope. Excluded from pool until gate clears.
- `Deferred` — explicitly postponed by the operator, not a blocker but not in the active sprint plan. Excluded from pool.

Agents picking the next ticket read this column first, then follow the sequencing recommendation at the end of the section. New tickets are created with `Status: Pending`.

| ID | Title | Status | Scope | Acceptance | Priority |
| --- | --- | --- | --- | --- | --- |
| `ENG-001` | E2E test harness | Partial | Add Playwright against the web app + embedded backend in headless Electron. Cover: login → open cash session → create sale (split tender) → refund → close session. **Step 1 shipped**: `npm run test:e2e:web` runs a Playwright web suite against the standalone backend and Vite app. Global-setup seeds an idempotent baseline (admin/manager/cashier/viewer template users plus a secondary active site) and prunes prior-run artefacts. **Step 2 shipped**: 16 business-flow tests cover sales (complete / refund / void + split-payment details), purchases (complete / return / void), stock adjustments, inter-site transfers (discrepancy + perfect-receipt + over-receipt-blocked), cash-session opening from zero, manual paid-in movements, and cash-session closures (overage / shortage / balanced). Together with the smoke and quotations slices the suite now runs 25 tests in parallel. Every test seeds unique actors and products (random UUID suffix on email, sku, register name) so the suite is fully parallelisable. Every test attaches a client issue tracker that fails the run on unexpected console errors / page errors / 4xx-5xx responses. A `data-row-id` attribute on DataTable rows lets tests pick specific rows deterministically under parallelism. See `e2e/README.md` for the operator guide. **Step 3 shipped**: baseline helpers extracted into `e2e/shared/baseline.ts` so both runners share the same user + site seeding; new `e2e/electron/` suite launches Electron via `_electron.launch()` against a pre-seeded tmpdir DB under `test-results/electron-userdata/` with a smoke test covering login → dashboard and zero-console-error invariant; new `playwright.electron.config.ts`; new root `test:e2e:electron` + `test:e2e` scripts; new `scripts/ensure-electron-main-build.mjs` guard fails fast with an actionable message when the Vite main bundle is absent. New `e2e-web` job in `ci.yml` runs the web suite on every PR with a cached Playwright browser binary keyed on the `package-lock.json` hash and uploads `playwright-report/web` always plus `test-results/playwright-web` on failure (traces, screenshots, videos; retention 7 days). **Remaining**: Electron-in-CI — requires xvfb on ubuntu + a packaged-binary build step that `ci:desktop` does not produce today. Captured as a follow-up; the Electron suite stays local-only until the first externally-signed installer approaches. | `npm run test:e2e` green in CI on Linux; screenshots on failure uploaded as CI artifact. | **High** |
| `ENG-002` | Versioned Drizzle migrations | Shipped | Generate baseline migration from current schema. Replace `runSchemaSync()` raw DDL bootstrap with `migrate()` on startup. Retain `IF NOT EXISTS` only as a one-time adoption shim for existing installs. **Step 1 shipped**: baseline migration (`src/db/migrations/0000_0000_baseline.sql`) captures the full current schema with dynamic `(datetime('now'))` defaults; `initDatabase()` runs `drizzleMigrate()` at boot guarded by an `existsSync` check on `meta/_journal.json`; `ensureMigrationBaseline()` seeds `__drizzle_migrations` on pre-ENG-002 DBs so the baseline is not re-run against an existing schema. **Step 2 shipped**: `DatabaseOptions` / `ServerOptions` now accept a `migrationsFolder` override; `apps/desktop/forge.config.ts` ships `packages/server/dist/db/migrations` via `extraResource`; `apps/desktop/src/main/index.ts` passes `process.resourcesPath/migrations` when `app.isPackaged`, so packaged Electron builds exercise the real migrator end-to-end. A new override-path integration test in `migrations.test.ts` locks the contract. **Step 3 shipped**: `runSchemaSync()` + the `ensureColumn()` / `createIndexIfColumnsExist()` helpers are gone; `packages/server/src/db/index.ts` shrank from 1,638 to 444 lines. `drizzleMigrate()` is now the single schema path — the missing-migrations-folder branch hard-throws an actionable error instead of silently falling back. Catalog seeds hoisted into a defensive `seedCatalogs()` hook gated by table existence, so adopted DBs that skip the transitional release log an actionable warning instead of crashing. A new `migrations-parity.test.ts` pins the invariant that `drizzleMigrate` alone produces the full schema; `migrations.test.ts` gained a missing-folder-throws assertion and an adopted-DB catalog-seed assertion; `db.seed.test.ts` legacy case rewritten to validate the adoption shim's column-preservation contract. | Adding a column requires only editing `schema.ts` + `drizzle-kit generate`; re-running against an existing DB is a no-op. | **High** |
| `ENG-003` | CI coverage threshold | Shipped | Run `vitest --coverage --run` in `ci:web` and `ci:server`. Fail the job below the thresholds declared in `vitest.config.ts`. Upload LCOV. **Shipped**: both workspaces now declare enforceable v8 coverage thresholds (server 80/80/77/63 statements/lines/functions/branches; web 65/65/68/60 — the web floor replaces the previously unenforced 70/70/70/70 declaration, because the suite had drifted below). `ci:web` and `ci:server` invoke the new `test:coverage` variant that passes `--coverage`, making thresholds actually gate. `lcov` reporter is wired into both configs and `.github/workflows/ci.yml` uploads `coverage/lcov.info` as an artifact for both jobs. Follow-up `ENG-003b` tracks raising the web floor back toward 70% via new component/route tests; it is a pure test-writing effort with no CI plumbing left to do. | PR lowering coverage below threshold fails CI. | **High** |
| `ENG-003b` | Raise web coverage back to 70% | Shipped | The web floor landed at 65/65/68/60 in ENG-003 to match the actual state of the suite at the time. Write new component + route tests to bring every axis back to 70% (statements/lines/functions/branches) and then raise the thresholds accordingly in `apps/web/vitest.config.ts`. Scope is test-writing only; no CI or config plumbing change. **Shipped**: 13 new test files + 6 extended existing files closed every axis. New: `roleAccess.test.ts`, `useElectron.test.ts`, `siteSelection.test.ts`, `siteStorage.test.ts`, `authStorage.test.ts`, `AuthProvider.test.tsx`, `TenantProvider.test.tsx`, `saleHistoryExport.test.ts`, `purchaseHistoryExport.test.ts`, `quotationHistoryExport.test.ts`, `useTableExport.test.ts`, `exportService.csv.test.ts`, `utils.test.ts`. Extended: `auditLogsExport.test.ts`, `pricing.test.ts`, `defaultLayouts.test.ts`, `providerState.test.ts`, `checkoutPayment.test.ts`, `saleCart.test.ts`. Final coverage 78.64 / 79.31 / 80.16 / 70.20 (statements / lines / functions / branches) — all four above the new 70/70/70/70 floor. Branches axis was the toughest gap (61.42 → 70.20) and drove most of the test surface. Pure test-writing per the AC; the only production-code change was a defensive collateral fix to `formatDate`/`formatDateTime` returning empty string on Invalid Date (their existing call sites would have thrown on null inputs, surfaced by the new export-utility tests). | All four axes ≥ 70% in `apps/web/vitest.config.ts`. | **Medium** |
| `ENG-004` | Electron main window sandbox | Shipped | Audit every `ipcMain` handler and preload export; remove Node-only APIs from the renderer path. Flip `sandbox: true` on the main `BrowserWindow`. **Shipped**: the security-critical webPreferences now live in `apps/desktop/src/main/window-config.ts` as a single-source-of-truth constant (`MAIN_WINDOW_WEB_PREFERENCES`), and `buildMainWindowWebPreferences()` constructs the exact `BrowserWindow` shape consumed by `main/index.ts`. The bridge audit confirmed every preload export is a pure `contextBridge → ipcRenderer.invoke` wrapper (four namespaces, 29 methods), so no preload refactor was needed. A node-test regression pin in `src/main/__tests__/window-config.test.ts` asserts `sandbox === true`, `contextIsolation === true`, `nodeIntegration === false`, and that the assembled `webPreferences` object passed to `BrowserWindow` keeps those flags intact; it is wired into `ci:desktop` — a tamper-check confirmed the test fails with a clear `ERR_ASSERTION` when any field is weakened. | App boots with `sandbox: true`; all renderer→main calls still pass; add regression test that asserts `webPreferences.sandbox === true`. | **High** |
| `ENG-005` | Desktop CI build matrix | Shipped | Extend `ci.yml` to run `npm run ci:desktop` on `ubuntu-latest`, `macos-latest`, `windows-latest`. Packaging step may stay in `release.yml`, but typecheck + lint + unit tests must run on all three. **Shipped**: the `desktop` job in `.github/workflows/ci.yml` now uses `strategy.matrix.os` on all three runners with `fail-fast: false` so one OS's break does not mask the others. The other jobs (web, backend, release-automation) stay on `ubuntu-latest` because ENG-005 scopes the matrix specifically to desktop — where native modules compile per-platform and cross-OS regressions historically hid until release time. A cross-platform audit of every script that `ci:desktop` invokes (root `package.json`, server/web/desktop workspace scripts, `packages/server/scripts/copy-migrations.mjs`, `scripts/ensure-native-runtime.mjs`) found zero POSIX-only hazards — the repo was already path-portable and `ensure-native-runtime.mjs` has explicit `process.platform === 'win32'` handling. `better-sqlite3@12.8.0` and `argon2` ship prebuilt binaries for linux-x64, darwin-x64, darwin-arm64, and win32-x64, so `npm ci` does not need a native toolchain on any runner. Packaging itself (`electron-forge make`, signing) remains in `release.yml` because it needs signing material the CI runners do not carry. | CI badge reflects all three OS; a PR that breaks a Windows-only path fails CI. | **Medium** |
| `ENG-006` | Structured logging | Shipped | Replace `console.log`/`console.error` calls in `packages/server` and `apps/desktop/src/main` with a `pino` logger, namespaced per module (`sales`, `sync`, `cash-session`, …). Redact PII (emails, passwords, tokens). **Shipped**: `packages/server/src/logging/logger.ts` exports `rootLogger` plus `createModuleLogger(name)` which returns a pino child tagged `module: <name>`. Fastify adopts the shared root logger when `verbose: true` so HTTP + app logs share one NDJSON stream. Two banner call sites keep plaintext on `process.stdout.write`: the standalone startup banner and the first-run admin credentials — both are one-shot operator UX and the credentials banner deliberately bypasses the structured stream so downstream aggregators cannot leak plaintext. | `ENG-008` | Auth hardening | Shipped | Rate-limit `auth.login` specifically (per IP and per username). Lock-out escalation after N failed attempts. Document the policy in `docs/SECURITY.md`. **Shipped**: `packages/server/src/security/loginRateLimit.ts` carries two in-memory TTL buckets — 10 attempts per IP per 60 seconds and 5 failed attempts per username per 15 minutes. Both buckets increment on every unauthorized branch (user not found, disabled user, wrong password, disabled tenant); a successful login clears the username bucket while the IP bucket decays via TTL so a single legitimate login cannot amnesty a stuffing source. `auth.login` throws `TOO_MANY_REQUESTS` with `errorCode: AUTH_RATE_LIMIT_EXCEEDED` and `details: { kind, key, max, secondsUntilReset }` when either cap is hit. 14 new tests (10 service units + 4 integration scenarios incl. the 50-bad-logins acceptance gate) join the suite. `docs/SECURITY.md` documents policy, attack coverage, and future hardening tracked as `ENG-008b` for DB-backed persistence. | Load test: 50 bad logins from one IP returns `429` before the 60-second window completes. | **Medium** |
| `ENG-008b` | Persistent login rate-limit state | Shipped | ENG-008 used in-memory buckets that a server restart wiped. Promote the `loginRateLimit` service to read/write from a `login_attempts` Drizzle table so multi-tenant cloud deployments survive restarts and can observe attack telemetry historically. Keep the current in-memory fast path as a cache to avoid DB round-trips per login attempt. **Shipped**: new `login_attempts` table (migration `0006_login_attempts.sql`) keyed on `(kind, key)` with an `expires_at` index — intentionally NOT tenant-scoped so one IP hammering many tenants still trips the global cap. `packages/server/src/security/loginRateLimit.ts` rewritten to accept a `DatabaseInstance` on every call, with the Maps demoted to a write-through cache (reads fall back to the DB, writes upsert the row first and then mirror the state). Adopted-DB safety: a table-existence check logs one warning and falls back to cache-only if `ensureMigrationBaseline()` pinned the journal before 0006 ran. 11 unit tests in `loginRateLimit.test.ts` exercise the full service against `:memory:`; new `loginRateLimit-persistence.test.ts` boots against a tmpdir file, saturates the username cap, restarts via `closeDatabase() + initDatabase()`, and asserts the next attempt still throws `AUTH_RATE_LIMIT_EXCEEDED`. `auth.test.ts` gains a DB-row assertion covering the persistence contract. | `ENG-032` | AI anomaly + fraud detection | Shipped | Local-only models (no LLM dependency): four sub-detectors implemented in `services/ai/anomalyDetection.ts` covering the five most common POS retail fraud patterns documented for LATAM SMB context — `ticketsPerHourSpike` (per-cashier vs personal 30-day baseline), `voidRate` (cross-cashier ratio outlier from `audit_logs.action='sale.void'`), `refundAmount` (top-K outlier amounts from `sale_returns`), `noSaleSessions` (zero-sale cash sessions over 30 minutes). Algorithm chose **z-score with leave-one-out baseline** over isolation forest: ~80 LOC, deterministic, defensible if a cashier disputes a flag, robust on small populations (5-15 cashiers) where vanilla z-score caps the outlier's own score around 2σ. Threshold 3σ entry, 4.5σ for `high` severity. Tunable constants exported via `anomalyDetectionConstants` for future per-tenant tuning. New `ai.anomalies.list` tRPC procedure (manager+) reuses `tenants.settings.ai.enabled` for short-circuit when the master switch is off — no `ai_audit_log` write because the detector is purely statistical. New `aiAnomalies` i18n namespace en + es (neutral LATAM tú). New dashboard tile `AnomalyDetectionCard` with five UX states (loading / error / disabled / empty / has-alerts with severity pills) plus `AnomalyDetailsModal` drill-down with kind filter and table. Read-only by design in v1; "investigate cashier" CTA captured as BACKLOG follow-up. New Spanish-language doc `docs/AI-ANOMALY-DETECTION.md` carries the full design rationale, the five fraud patterns with examples, the privacy-driven local-only justification (Habeas Data CO, LFPDPPP MX, Ley 19.628 CL), and the upgrade criteria for migrating to isolation forest if pilot data warrants. **Shipped**: 10 detector unit tests with synthetic fixtures + narrative comments in Spanish; 5 `ai.anomalies.list` integration tests via createCaller (cashier FORBIDDEN, ai.enabled=false short-circuit, valid shape with enabled, from>to BAD_REQUEST, cross-tenant isolation); 5 dashboard card render tests (loading / disabled / empty / has-alerts / error). | Synthetic anomaly fixture triggers alert; clean baseline does not; multi-tenant isolation tested; cashier role does not see other cashiers' anomalies (manager+ only). | **Medium** |

| `ENG-037` | libSQL/Turso embedded replicas spike | Shipped | 1-week investigation + 3-4 week implementation if greenlit. Adds read-replica + automatic cloud backup pattern without migrating off SQLite. Closes the multi-site sync gap referenced in `PLAN.md` §10. The spike report itself is the deliverable for the first week; if greenlit, the implementation lands in the same ticket. **Shipped 2026-05-08**: spike report committed at [`docs/SPIKE-LIBSQL-TURSO.md`](./SPIKE-LIBSQL-TURSO.md). Recommendation: **Defer (revisit after Phase 4)**. Three findings drive the call — (1) legacy Embedded Replicas are cloud-primary by default and conflict with ADR-0001 Local Store Authority; (2) current Turso Sync is still a beta surface whose documented conflict model is Last-Push-Wins, incompatible with Puntovivo's manual lane for money/fiscal/audit/cash/inventory data; (3) libSQL as a pure SQLite engine swap has not proven a simpler Electron 41 / Node 22 native runtime than `better-sqlite3`. The bespoke `sync_outbox` pipeline (ENG-064 + ENG-064b) plus a separate cloud-backup destination is the natural Phase 3+ shape. Reopen triggers documented in spike §2 (Turso Sync GA + manual-resolution API + proven native-runtime simplification or operator-reported `sync_outbox` shortcoming on a real central-server pilot). Implementation acceptance criteria preserved in spike §12 if any trigger fires. | Spike report committed (decision document); if greenlit, embedded replica works against Turso staging with conflict-resolution strategy documented and a fallback to local-only when offline. | **Medium** |

| `ENG-038c` | Reconciliation cron + 30-day fixture + AI tie-break matcher | Shipped | Carved out from the parent `ENG-038` so the matcher half of the AC could ship without waiting on live-provider contracts. **Shipped 2026-05-13**: new `services/payments/payment-worker.ts` mirrors the fiscal worker shape with two timers (Timer A — outbox housekeeping + stale-claim sweep every 30 s; Timer B — statement import every 2 h walking every (tenant, rail)) plus an explicit catch-up on boot that compares `tenants.settings.payments.<railId>.lastImportedAt` against a 12 h threshold and dispatches a single import for the missing window before either timer's first tick. First-boot tenants (no marker) start with a 30-day lookback. Live charge dispatch (queued → submitting → approved) stays deferred to the rail-specific API clients ticket; Timer A keeps the housekeeping plumbing warm so the future slice plugs in a `dispatchCharge` callback without rewiring the worker shell. `setDefaultPaymentWorker` wires the singleton from `createServer`; `listen()` starts both timers and fires `catchUpOnBoot()` after the workers arm. Webhook-push ingestion stays out of scope — POS desktop has no public IP, so the pull canal is the v1 path until a central server retransmits webhooks. New `services/payments/reconciliation.ts::runReconciliationPass` walks an injected batch of statement rows, classifies each via the existing deterministic taxonomy (`amount_mismatch` / `missing_provider_reference` / `orphan_provider_row` / `provider_issue`) plus a new `ambiguous` kind for cases where ≥ 2 candidates still tie after the strict pass, and writes matched outbox rows to `status='settled'` with the provider transaction id. The pre-existing `getPaymentReconciliation` read-only query stays untouched — it still powers the Operations Center panel. New `services/payments/ai-tiebreak.ts` hands the ambiguous bucket to the configured language provider via `generateObject` against a tight Zod schema (`pickedSalePaymentId, confidence, explanation`); every short-circuit (`ai-disabled`, `ai-budget-exceeded`, `ai-not-implemented`, `ai-provider-error`, `ai-not-decisive`) degrades silently to a deterministic `suggestedAction='review_provider'` mismatch so the cron never throws. Three new error codes (`PAYMENT_RECONCILIATION_NO_MATCH`, `PAYMENT_RECONCILIATION_AMBIGUOUS`, `PAYMENT_RECONCILIATION_AI_DEGRADED`) ship en + es in neutral LATAM `tú` register. `AIFeature` union extends with `paymentReconciliation`; both success and degraded paths land an `ai_audit_log` row so the operator's monthly spend + breakdown aggregates remain accurate. New `__fixtures__/payment-statements/index.ts` exports a deterministic mulberry32-seeded generator producing 6 rails × 30 days × 6 settlements/day = 1068 statement rows with a 5% controlled mismatch rate sprinkled evenly across the four classifier types — both halves of the seed (provider statement rows + POS-side outbox / tender rows) are derived together so tests and the benchmark stay in lockstep. Three new test files: `payments-matcher.test.ts` (6 cases — 95% AC proof, classifier coverage, settled status mirror, AI tie-break decisive + degraded paths, multi-tenant isolation); `payment-worker.test.ts` (9 cases — stale sweep, fresh-row no-touch, fetcher-missing returns `skippedReason='fetcher-missing'`, fetcher-success advances marker, fetcher-failure leaves marker untouched, statement walking, three catch-up branches: first-boot / gap-above-threshold / gap-below-threshold); `payments-ai-tiebreak.test.ts` (4 gating short-circuits: AI off, budget zero, budget exhausted, empty settings). New operator-runnable `npm run benchmark:payment-reconciliation` script (modeled on `benchmark:invoice-ocr`): 96.63% match rate in 32 ms against the seed=7 fixture (above the 95% threshold; exits non-zero below). ci:server 1615 / 1615 tests pass at coverage 84.67/71.33/81.05/85.87 (above 80/63/77/80 floor); ci:web 1002 / 1002 tests pass (above 70/70/70/70 floor; three new error keys passed locale-parity). Live smoke validated `/operations?tab=payments` continues to render cleanly — the panel stays read-only in this slice; the admin retry/requeue + per-method breakdown UI is carved out for ENG-065d. | Reconciliation cron correctly matches 95%+ of synthetic statement rows on the 30-day fixture; ambiguous candidates flow through the AI tie-break with graceful degradation when the provider is unavailable; the worker boots a catch-up sweep at start so an offline POS reconciles missed windows. | **High** |

Both resolver paths now read `provider.defaultEmbeddingModelId ?? DEFAULT_EMBEDDING_MODEL` so each provider's canonical model id flows through; the legacy constant stays for backwards-compat. Dimension drift (768-d Ollama vs 1536-d OpenAI) is intentionally not auto-handled — `cosineSimilarity` already returns 0 for mismatched dims, so the worst case is an incomplete result list (not wrong matches) and the operator clicks "Regenerate embeddings" after switching providers (same constraint as switching between OpenAI's small + large models). 3 test updates (ollama.test.ts flipped from "stays undefined" to assert the embedding factory + cross-checks the default against the exported `FALLBACK_EMBEDDING_MODEL_ID`; openai.test.ts gains a `defaultEmbeddingModelId === 'text-embedding-3-small'` assertion). | `ENG-042` | Sync resilience UX (stale conflicts + network errors) | Shipped | Out-of-band Phase-0-adjacent ticket opened to document an already-implemented body of work covering three concerns at once: (1) the sync conflict UI used to render `entityType · entityId` snake_case pills and stall the queue forever when the local row had been deleted server-side; (2) the embedded server returned `Failed to fetch` text directly to operators on transient network drops, mostly during the AuthProvider boot path; (3) Company* card error toasts surfaced raw `error.message` instead of the localized `errors:server.*` copy. **Shipped**: server `sync.listConflicts` + `sync.pull` now expose `localRecordExists: boolean | null` per item / conflict by probing `findEntity` against the active tenant scope; `sync.resolve` refuses `keepLocal` and `merged` when the local row is missing and steers the operator to `acceptRemote` (rebadged as "Discard Local Change" in the UI). New `apps/web/src/features/company/companySyncDisplay.ts` maps internal entity types + operations to localized labels via a `company.sync.entities.*` / `operations.*` namespace and turns the server `lastError` text into a translated hint via `getSyncQueueIssueMessage`. The Pending Queue and Conflicts cards now render an "Item title" plus a collapsible "Technical details" disclosure (entity type + id + operation + raw error stay accessible without dominating the card). Conflict modal copy moved from interpolating `entityType` + `entityId` into prose to interpolating a localized `entity` label across three dialog variants (keep local / accept remote / discard stale local change). `translateServerError` gains `isNetworkConnectivityError` (matches `Failed to fetch`, `fetch failed`, `Load failed`, `NetworkError when attempting to fetch resource.` recursively across `cause` chains) plus a new `errors:server.networkUnavailable` key in en + es so the AuthProvider boot path no longer logs raw fetch failures and every Company card surfaces a friendly hint when the embedded server is unreachable. Header layout tightened so the language and site selectors share a consistent baseline alignment across viewport widths. Tests: `sync.test.ts` covers the missing-local rejection path and asserts `localRecordExists` is exposed on `pull` and `listConflicts`; `CompanySyncCard.test.tsx` adds a missing-local conflict scenario that asserts the disabled buttons, the discard CTA copy, and the resolve mutation payload; `translateServerError.test.ts` covers `TypeError('Failed to fetch')`, the wrapped tRPC error with `cause`, and the missing-key fallback. `npm audit --omit=dev` stays at 0 high; `ci:web` + `ci:server` green. **Shipped (ENG-042 close-out)**: the two `[infra][sync]` follow-ups previously captured as working title `ENG-043` landed in a single TOCTOU sweep: (a) `sync.resolve` `findEntity` guard hoisted INSIDE `ctx.db.transaction(...)` so a concurrent delete between the precondition check and the transaction body can no longer leave keepLocal / merged paths resolving against stale data — better-sqlite3 transactions are connection-scoped so calling `findEntity(ctx.db, ...)` from inside the callback runs against the same in-flight BEGIN; (b) the prose `error.message` `"Cannot keep or merge local changes…"` was replaced with `throwServerError({ errorCode: 'SYNC_LOCAL_RECORD_MISSING', ... })`, registered in both `packages/server/src/lib/errorCodes.ts` and `apps/web/src/lib/translateServerError.ts::KNOWN_SERVER_ERROR_CODES`, with neutral LATAM Spanish copy `"El registro local ya no existe. Descarta el cambio local para aceptar la versión remota."` and the English equivalent landing in `apps/web/src/i18n/locales/{en,es}/errors.json`. Audit-driven scope expansion (operator-approved): the same TOCTOU shape was found at three `sales.ts` sites where `requireActiveCashSession` runs BEFORE `ctx.db.transaction(...)` and `activeCashSession.id` is then written as the FK inside; new module-private `assertCashSessionStillOpen(tx, tenantId, cashSessionId)` helper added with `CASH_SESSION_REQUIRED` re-validation as the FIRST statement inside `sales.create`, `sales.returnSale`, and `sales.completeDraft` transactions. Tests: 2 new `sync.test.ts` cases pin the new errorCode shape and no-partial-write behavior (conflict status stays `pending`, queue row survives); the existing missing-local rejection test was updated to assert on `cause.errorCode` instead of the now-changed prose. Coverage: server 84.19/68.46/81.06/85.09 (above the 80 floor); web locale-parity green. | `ENG-057` | Fiscal outbox + contingency engine | Shipped | Introduce a fiscal outbox separate from generic sync with queued/submitting/accepted/rejected/contingency/retrying/dead-letter lifecycle, retry backoff, normalized provider errors, and operator-visible recovery. **Shipped**: migración `0013_fiscal_outbox.sql` agrega la primera tabla concreta consumiendo el outbox kernel de ENG-053 — `fiscal_outbox` con 7-state status enum (`queued/submitting/accepted/rejected/contingency/retrying/dead_letter`), kind enum tightened a `['emit']` (cancel/retry_contingency/fetch_status diferidos per ADR-0003 sequencing), tres índices (`tenant_status_retry`, `fiscal_document`, `tenant_created`). Schema mirror: `fiscalOutboxStatusEnum` + `fiscalOutboxKindEnum` exports. Nuevo módulo `services/fiscal/errors.ts` con `FiscalProviderError` class + closed `NormalizedFiscalErrorKind` union de 10 kinds (4 recoverable: NETWORK_TIMEOUT/PROVIDER_5XX/RATE_LIMITED/UNKNOWN; 6 non-recoverable: PROVIDER_4XX/PROVIDER_REJECTED/MALFORMED_REQUEST/INVALID_CERT/EXPIRED_CERT/AUTH_FAILED). `services/fiscal/error-normalizer.ts` con `normalizeFiscalError(err, providerId)` dispatch a per-pack mappers + default heuristic (TypeError/SyntaxError → MALFORMED_REQUEST non-recoverable; everything else → PROVIDER_5XX recoverable). 3 stub mappers `packs/{co,mx,cl}/error-mapping.ts` retornan null para que el normalizer caiga al default heuristic — provider-specific code dispatch llega incrementalmente con ENG-021/ENG-035c/ENG-036c. Orchestrator `services/fiscal/orchestrator.ts` ahora exporta `enqueueFiscalEmission(args)` que en una sola tx local: idempotency probe en `(tenantId, source, sourceId, kind)`, validateConfig pre-flight (paquetes parqueados como MX sin RFC retornan null sin escribir fila — preserva legacy behavior), resolución de buyer/lines/resolution/locale/tenantSettings, INSERT `fiscal_documents` con `status='pending'` + CUFE placeholder `pending-<nanoid>` (la tabla unique constraint queda satisfecha por el random nanoid; el worker overwrite con el CUFE real del adapter en accepted), INSERT `fiscal_document_items`, advance `fiscal_numbering_resolutions.currentNumber`, INSERT `fiscal_outbox` row con payload completo `{countryCode, providerId, fiscalDocumentId, adapterInput}`. Después del commit hace fire-and-forget `tickDefaultFiscalWorker(tenantId)` para que happy-path latency esté cerca del status quo síncrono. Back-compat shim `safelyEmitFiscalDocument` ahora delega a `enqueueFiscalEmission` retornando la legacy `{id, cufe, documentNumber, status}` shape — los tres callers (`completeSale.ts`, `voidSale.ts`, `returnSale.ts`) no requirieron ediciones. `emitFiscalDocument` legacy permanece para los tests existentes que la invocan directamente. Nuevo daemon `services/fiscal/fiscal-worker.ts`: factory `createFiscalWorker({db, tenantIdsProvider, intervalMs, workerId, retryPolicy, resolveAdapter})` retorna `{tickOnce, start, stop}`. Boot wired en `index.ts::createServer` como singleton via `setDefaultFiscalWorker`, registered en `app.addHook('onClose')`, expuesto en `PuntovivoServer.fiscalWorker` para tests. Tick cadence: 30s setInterval + immediate `tickOnce` después de enqueue + stale-claim sweep a startup AND cada 5 min + per-tick adapter timeout 60s. Mirror invariant: en éxito worker UPDATE `fiscal_documents` (status='accepted', cufe real, providerResponse, xmlRef) ANTES del kernel transition; en recoverable error UPDATE doc to status='contingency' → outbox status='retrying' o 'dead_letter' al exhaustion; en non-recoverable error UPDATE doc to status='rejected' → outbox status='dead_letter' inmediato. Test seam `__setFiscalAdapterForTest(countryCode, adapter)` + `__clearFiscalAdapterOverridesForTest()` en `services/fiscal/registry.ts` permite inyectar stubs con `throwOracle?: (input) => Error \| undefined` (extensión simétrica del existente `contingencyOracle` en MockAdapter). Nueva admin tRPC procedure `reports.fiscal.retryDocument({fiscalDocumentId})`: re-arma rows en `retrying`/`contingency` (clear nextRetryAt) o re-enqueue rows en `dead_letter`/`rejected` (insert fresh outbox row con priority=-1 + reset doc status to `pending`); ambas paths fire `tickOnce` para drain inmediato. 6 integration tests nuevos en `__tests__/fiscal-outbox-integration.test.ts` cubriendo los 4 acceptance paths (happy → outbox=accepted + doc=accepted, recoverable outage → outbox=retrying + doc=contingency + sale completed sin rollback, non-recoverable error → outbox=dead_letter + doc=rejected, retry router rearm → next tick drains a accepted) + integration con pendingChecks (contingency rows count, rejected rows excluded) + retry dead-letter idempotente post-accepted. Server 969 tests verde, coverage 83.6/69.7/79.89/84.78 (≥ 80/63/77/80). Web 727 tests verde sin breakage de tRPC inference. Live smoke OK: dev:server boots, `fiscal_outbox` table presente con 3 índices, health endpoint responde. Counter Foundation Reset sube de 7/21 a 8/21. UI surface para retry button en `FiscalDocumentListPage` queda diferido — el operator puede llamar `reports.fiscal.retryDocument` via tRPC dev tools, y ENG-058/ENG-065 landearán la affordance proper. ENG-059 sigue gated en el real DIAN PT contract — el swap será una sola edición de `packs/co/index.ts` cuando el contract lande. | Offline sale completes locally and leaves a visible pending fiscal document; simulated provider outage writes contingency state and does not roll back the sale. | **High** |

Cuando `isResumedCart` es true, info-toast en lugar de silent drop. Nuevo daemon `services/peripherals/hardware-worker.ts` mirror de `services/fiscal/fiscal-worker.ts`: `createHardwareOutboxKernel(retryPolicy)` factory + `createHardwareWorker({db, tenantIdsProvider, intervalMs=30s, workerId, retryPolicy=BOUNDED_EXPONENTIAL_BACKOFF})`; tick cadence stale-claim sweep + periodic per-tenant fan-out con cap MAX_PER_TENANT_PER_TICK=25; `loadActivePeripheralForKind(siteId, targetKind)` resuelve printer vs drawer; dispatch por `kind` (`print-*` → ReceiptPrinterAdapter.print, `kick-drawer` → CashDrawerAdapter.kick); `toOutboxError` normaliza `NormalizedHardwareError → NormalizedOutboxError` (DEVICE_OFFLINE/DEVICE_TIMEOUT/PROTOCOL_ERROR/UNKNOWN recoverable; INVALID_CONFIG/DRIVER_NOT_IMPLEMENTED/PERMISSION_DENIED non-recoverable); boot-wired en `index.ts::createServer` paralelo al fiscal worker via `setDefaultHardwareWorker` + `app.addHook('onClose')`. Tres procedures tRPC nuevas en `routers/peripherals.ts`: `printReceipt({saleId, siteId})` `tenantProcedure` carga sale via `getSaleRecord` (cross-tenant guard) + valida site + lee active printer; cuando no hay row OR driver=system retorna `{status: 'system-fallback'}` (renderer keeps owning HTML); cuando driver=escpos llama `adapter.print(job)` con structured `ReceiptDocument` derivado de `buildSaleReceiptDocument(sale, ...)`; on success `{status: 'printed'}`, on error enqueue `hardware_outbox` row con kind=print-receipt + retry policy + fire-and-forget `tickDefaultHardwareWorker` y retorna `{status: 'fallback', error, errorMessage}` para que el renderer caiga al legacy HTML path AND emita toast traducido; `kickCashDrawer({siteId})` `managerOrAdminProcedure` carga active drawer; sin drawer registrado retorna `{status: 'no-drawer-registered'}` (UI hides the button — no toast); on success `{status: 'ok'}`, on error enqueue retry row (idempotente) + retorna `{status: 'error'}`; `peekHardwareOutbox({limit?})` `managerOrAdminProcedure` retorna minimal projection del outbox tail tenant-scoped, stub para que ENG-065 (Operations Center) lo consuma. Tres error codes nuevos en `lib/errorCodes.ts`: `HARDWARE_SALE_NOT_FOUND`, `HARDWARE_NO_DRAWER_REGISTERED`, `HARDWARE_TRANSPORT_FAILED`. Renderer wiring (Option A surgical, NO new IPC bridge — ESC/POS dispatch es SERVER-SIDE en main process via tRPC + native `net.Socket`): `apps/web/src/features/sales/receiptPrinter.ts::printSaleReceipt(sale, options?)` extendido con `escposDispatcher?` callback + `onEscposFallback?` hook; el dispatcher llama `trpc.peripherals.printReceipt.mutate({saleId, siteId})` y rama por `result.status`: `printed` → done; `system-fallback` → seguir al legacy `window.electron.printReceipt(html)` path (silent); `fallback` → seguir al legacy AND llamar `onEscposFallback` que dispara toast `La impresora ESC/POS falló; imprimimos por la del sistema`. Existing `apps/desktop/src/main/index.ts:1933 ipcMain.handle('print-receipt')` UNTOUCHED; preload UNTOUCHED. `SaleDetailsModal.tsx` usa `useTenant().currentSite` + builds the dispatcher closure + pasa a ambos call sites de `printSaleReceipt` (manual print + reprint). `SalesOverview.tsx` extendido con optional `onKickCashDrawer?` + `isKickingCashDrawer?` props; el botón `Abrir cajón` con `data-testid="sales-kick-drawer"` aparece junto a `Registrar movimiento` y `Cerrar caja` solo cuando (a) user.role manager/admin, (b) hay un drawer escpos registrado. SalesPage compute el handler condicional + onSuccess toast diferenciado (`Cajón monedero abierto` / `No hay cajón monedero registrado` / `No se pudo abrir el cajón monedero`). Decisiones de scope: (1) **Native deps deferred** — `node-thermal-printer` + `usb` NOT installed; el byte-builder es pure JS y el transport ships con Mock + TCP (no native deps). USB + serial son stubs que arrojan `DRIVER_NOT_IMPLEMENTED`; un follow-up agrega los native bindings cuando el lab físico esté online. ci:server stays portable sin electron-rebuild. (2) **Server-side ESC/POS dispatch** (NO new IPC bridge): el escpos adapter abre USB/TCP desde el embedded Fastify in-process — el preload + `print-receipt` IPC handler quedan untouched. ENG-058's qrcode dynamic-import path stays intact. (3) **Auto-kick on cash sale parqueado**: ENG-062 ships solo el manual button + procedure; auto-kick on payment completion es follow-up cuando el operator confirme el UX. (4) **Server-side HTML fallback NOT shipped**: server retorna `{status:'system-fallback'}` signal only; el renderer sigue dueño de `buildSaleReceiptHtml`. Avoids HTML dual-source. (5) **Physical-hardware acceptance gated on test lab**: la acceptance "ESC/POS bytes print, cut, and open drawer in hardware smoke" se cumple a nivel byte (24 + 8 + 9 tests + smoke con mock); printer físico + drawer físico stay como follow-up smoke cuando el lab esté online. (6) **`hardware_outbox` deferral closed**: ADR-0003 footer "Updated 2026-05-04 (ENG-060): hardware_outbox deferred to ENG-062" eliminado; la tabla y el worker existen ahora. (7) **`escpos` driver picker para `cash_drawer`**: el config slot mirror del printer (channel + host/port/etc.) — operador apunta ambos al mismo physical hardware; JSDoc en `EscPosCashDrawerAdapter` lo documenta. | `ENG-064` | Sync contract v1 | Shipped | Formalize sync payload contract with entity type, operation, payload version, idempotency key, device ID, priority, dependencies, ordering, retry, duplicate suppression, and conflict policy. **Shipped**: migración `0016_sync_contract_v1.sql` agrega tabla `sync_outbox` (mirror estructural de `fiscal_outbox` ENG-057 / `hardware_outbox` ENG-062 con kernel projection — `id, tenantId, status, payload, payloadVersion, attempts, nextRetryAt, lastError, priority, claimToken, lockedAt, createdAt, updatedAt`) PLUS las 7 columnas de contrato per ADR-0002/0003/0004: `entityType, entityId, operation, conflictPolicy, idempotencyKey, deviceId, dependsOnOperationId, operationEventId`. Status enum `queued/submitting/synced/conflict/retrying/dead_letter`. Cuatro índices: `(tenant, status, nextRetry)` para el claimNext del kernel, `(entityType, entityId)` para drilldown del Operations Center, `(tenant, createdAt)` para listing, y partial unique `(tenant, entityType, entityId, operation, idempotencyKey) WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL` que colapsa retries idempotentes en una sola fila. Data migration one-shot `INSERT OR IGNORE INTO sync_outbox SELECT ... FROM sync_queue` copia las pending rows con defaults sensatos (`payloadVersion=1`, `priority=0`) y aplica `conflictPolicy='manual'` para las 16 entidades de ADR-0004 high-risk (sales/sale_*/cash_*/fiscal_*/inventory_*/transfer_*/stock_adjustments/audit_logs), `auto_lww` para todo lo demás (catalog + preferences). Schema bump: `syncOutboxStatusEnum`, `syncConflictPolicyEnum`, `syncOperationEnum` (TS-only narrowing). Pure manifest en `services/sync/contract.ts` con `SYNC_PAYLOAD_VERSION=1`, `SYNC_ENTITY_TYPES` (45 entidades exhaustivas), `SYNC_CONFLICT_POLICY: Record<SyncEntityType, 'manual' | 'auto_lww'>` exhaustivo, `resolveConflictPolicy(entityType)` defense-in-depth runtime guard, `resolveDefaultPriority` (audit_logs=10, money-bound=5, catalog=0), `buildSyncContractManifest()` para `sync.getContract`. Helper `services/sync/enqueue.ts` con `enqueueSync(ctx, args)` que reemplaza el inline `db.insert(syncQueue).values(...)` pattern: lee envelope context (`ctx.envelope?.{operationId, idempotencyKey}` + `ctx.deviceId` inyectados por ENG-052's `commandEnvelope` middleware), resuelve `operation_event_id` via lookup en `operation_events` por `(tenantId, operationId)`, popula el contrato, escribe una fila a `sync_outbox` + emite `operation_effects` `kind=outbox_enqueue:sync` para el journal trail (ENG-053). Captura UNIQUE constraint failures del partial unique idempotent index y retorna `{id, deduped: true}` en lugar de throw — retries de la misma envelope colapsan a una sola fila. Tres procedures tRPC nuevas en `routers/sync.ts` (additivas — los 8 procedures existentes operan sobre `sync_queue` sin cambio): `sync.getContract` (managerOrAdmin) retorna `{payloadVersion, entities: Array<{entityType, conflictPolicy, defaultPriority}>}` desde el manifest para que ENG-068+ multi-store sync negocie el contrato; `sync.peekOutbox({limit})` (managerOrAdmin) projection minimal del tail de `sync_outbox` ordenada por `(priority DESC, createdAt ASC)` para que ENG-065 Operations Center renderice manual conflicts distintos; `sync.retry({id})` (admin) operator path para "esta fila se atascó, force retry now" — re-arma solo rows `retrying`/`dead_letter` reseteando `attempts=0`, `nextRetryAt=null`, `lastError=null`, `claimToken=null`, status back to `queued`; `queued`/`submitting`/`synced`/`conflict` son no-op para no replayear rows drenados; surfaces `SYNC_OUTBOX_NOT_FOUND` cuando el row id es foreign. Dos error codes nuevos en `lib/errorCodes.ts`: `SYNC_OUTBOX_NOT_FOUND`, `SYNC_OUTBOX_DEAD_LETTER`. Nueva ADR `docs/architecture/0005-sync-payload-contract.md` documenta el manifest + version-bump protocol + sync_outbox schema; cross-link agregado en `docs/architecture/README.md`; `docs/PLAN.md §18.1` registra el archivo. ADR-0003 footer "ENG-064 introduces sync_outbox and deprecates sync_queue" actualizado a "Shipped 2026-05-05" con nota explícita de que el writer rewrite + procedure cutover quedan parqueados a ENG-064b. 27 tests nuevos: `sync-contract-manifest.test.ts` (8 cases — payloadVersion positive, manifest keys match SYNC_ENTITY_TYPES, manual list (16 entidades) y auto_lww list (15 entidades) clasifican correctamente, resolveConflictPolicy throws on unknown, resolveDefaultPriority audit=10/money=5/catalog=0, manifest build con todas las entradas, exhaustiveness scan automated del entityType: '...' literal en cada router file que verifica zero drift) + `sync-contract-v1.test.ts` (19 cases cubriendo las 4 áreas de acceptance — Ordering: peekOutbox ordena audit_logs > sales > products por priority+createdAt; resolveDefaultPriority constants check; dependsOnOperationId persiste; Retry: sync.retry resetea attempts/nextRetryAt/lastError/status para retrying/dead_letter, no-op para synced, NOT_FOUND on unknown id, FORBIDDEN on cashier role, peekOutbox surfaces attempts+nextRetryAt; Duplicate suppression: idempotent retries con misma envelope key colapsan via partial unique idx, missing idempotencyKey produce filas separadas (catalog idempotent on consumer side), distintas keys producen filas separadas, cross-tenant isolation con shared key produce filas separadas; Manual conflict: 8 high-risk entities tagged manual, 5 catalog entities tagged auto_lww, peekOutbox surfaces conflictPolicy distinguible por entityType, runtime guard rechaza unknown entityType, admin can call getContract, cashier FORBIDDEN). Server 1135 tests verde, coverage 82.75/69.02/78.11/83.87 (≥ 80/63/77/80 floor). Web 768 tests verde sin cambios (todo el ticket es server-side). SQL-level smoke confirmó migration aplicada cleanly + las 4 indexes presentes. Counter Foundation Reset sube de 12/21 a 13/21. Decisiones de scope explícitas: (1) **Writer rewrite parqueado a ENG-064b**: los 19 router files (sales, cashSessions, purchases, orders, quotations, customers, products, categories, units, providers, vatRates, customerCatalogs, locations, sites, companies, sequentials, inventory, users, receiptTemplates) siguen usando `db.insert(syncQueue).values(...)` inline. ENG-064 v1 ships solo el HELPER + las nuevas procedures + los tests; cuando ENG-064b cierre, los 19 routers cambian a `enqueueSync(ctx, args)` y `sync.*` procedures corten a `sync_outbox`. La razón: el rewrite del 731-line `routers/sync.ts` + los 19 router edits son ~12h adicionales que pueden landear en una segunda pasada sin afectar la acceptance criteria, que solo requiere "Tests cover ordering, retry, duplicate suppression, and manual conflict paths for high-risk entities". (2) **Auto-LWW resolution behavior parqueado**: ENG-064 v1 ships solo el MARKER (`conflictPolicy='auto_lww'` en la fila); la lógica que aplica last-write-wins automáticamente en `sync.push` queda para ENG-064b o ENG-067. (3) **`sync_queue` legacy stays**: la tabla legacy sigue en place como deprecated read-only backstop hasta que ENG-064b la dropee post-cutover. (4) **No sync worker daemon**: ENG-064 v1 NO agrega un periodic worker — `sync.push` sigue siendo operator-triggered. ENG-066 chaos suite + ENG-068+ multi-store agregarán el daemon cuando el server-to-server sync arrive. (5) **No web changes**: `useOfflineSync.ts` + IndexedDB shadow stay untouched — el response shape de las procedures existentes sigue backward-compatible. ENG-065 Operations Center surface es el primer consumer del nuevo `peekOutbox`. **ENG-064b Shipped 2026-05-05** — see row below; cierra la cutover, dropea `sync_queue`, y elimina la colisión de nombre con el cliente IndexedDB. | Tests cover ordering, retry, duplicate suppression, and manual conflict paths for high-risk entities. | **High** |
| `ENG-064b` | Sync writer cutover + drop `sync_queue` | Shipped | Cierra la reescritura writer + cutover de procedures que ENG-064 dejó explicitamente parqueada: rutea cada `db.insert(syncQueue).values(...)` por `enqueueSync(ctx, args)`, corta las 8 procedures legacy `sync.*` (`status`, `listQueue`, `addToQueue`, `removeFromQueue`, `push`, `pull`, `resolve`, `listConflicts`) a `sync_outbox`, dropea `sync_queue`, y renombra el cliente web `services/storage/syncQueue.ts` → `offlineQueue.ts` para eliminar la colisión visual con la tabla server. **Shipped**: writer rewrite landed across 19 server router files (`categories`, `companies`, `customerCatalogs`, `customers`, `geography`, `inventory`, `locations`, `logos`, `orders`, `products`, `providers`, `purchases`, `sales`, `sequentials`, `sites`, `units`, `users`, `vatRates`, plus `sync.addToQueue` thin shim) + 4 application services (`completeSale`, `discardDraft`, `returnSale`, `voidSale`) + 1 dev seed (`seed-mega/historical-sync.ts` writes `sync_outbox` directly without envelope context for bulk performance). Para los writers tx-scoped, los inserts pasan POST-tx como `await enqueueSync(ctx, ...)` para preservar el callback síncrono de better-sqlite3 — la atomicidad de las entity rows se conserva; el sync_outbox enqueue corre post-commit y es idempotente vía el partial unique index si la misma envelope retry. El journal effect `sync_queue_emit` se retiró: `enqueueSync` escribe su propio efecto `outbox_enqueue:sync` vía `recordEffect` cuando hay envelope, así que los `effects.push({kind:'sync_queue_emit'...})` post-tx en los 4 sale lifecycle services se borraron. `routers/sync.ts` cutover: `sync.status` aggregates flip a `sync_outbox` con `status IN ('queued','submitting','retrying')` para pending count, `status='retrying'` para retry count, y `status IN ('retrying','dead_letter') AND lastError IS NOT NULL` para failed count; `sync.listQueue` + `sync.pull` aliasean `payload→data` y `payloadVersion→localVersion` en la projection para que `useOfflineSync.ts` siga consumiendo la misma shape; `sync.addToQueue` se vuelve thin shim de `enqueueSync`; `sync.removeFromQueue` borra de `sync_outbox`; `sync.push` reclama rows `status IN ('queued','retrying')` ordenado por `(priority DESC, createdAt ASC)`, transitions a `synced` en éxito y a `retrying` (con `lastError={kind:'UNKNOWN', message}`) en fallo — el helper legacy `incrementQueueFailure` se renombró a `markOutboxFailure`; `sync.resolve` UPDATEa `sync_outbox` a estado limpio y re-enqueue vía `enqueueSync` en vez de inline insert; `sync.listConflicts` queda untouched (la tabla `sync_conflicts` es su propia tabla). Migración `0017_drop_sync_queue.sql` dropea la tabla legacy con `DROP TABLE IF EXISTS sync_queue` (data ya backfilled a `sync_outbox` por el `0016` de ENG-064). `schema.ts` remueve `syncQueue` table + relations + types `SyncQueueItem`/`NewSyncQueueItem`; el JSDoc del outbox circundante se reescribe en past tense capturando el cutover. Web rename `apps/web/src/services/storage/syncQueue.ts` → `offlineQueue.ts` renombra archivo + clarifica JSDoc que esto es el buffer offline IndexedDB (independiente del server-side sync_outbox); el nombre interno del IndexedDB ObjectStore (`STORE_NAMES.SYNC_QUEUE`) se preserva para evitar version bump del DB cliente y migración de datos en devices existentes; imports actualizados en `StorageProvider.tsx`, `offlineStorage.ts`, `services/storage/index.ts`. Tests: 5 fixture inserts en `sync.test.ts` reshape de `data/localVersion` a `payload/payloadVersion/status/conflictPolicy`, `from(syncQueue)` flippea a `from(syncOutbox)` en todos los reads, `incrementQueueFailure`-driven assertions ahora esperan JSON `lastError` shape; `orders.test.ts` (3 sites), `purchases.test.ts` (3 sites), `application-sales-completeSale.test.ts` (4 sites), `application-sales-returnSale.test.ts` (kinds + test name), `application-sales-voidSale.test.ts` (kinds), `application-sales-discardDraft.test.ts` (kinds) — todos flippean refs `syncQueue` → `syncOutbox` y journal kind `sync_queue_emit` → `outbox_enqueue:sync`. `seed-mega/types.ts` + `seed-mega/index.ts` renombran `syncQueueRows` → `syncOutboxRows` y `syncQueuePending` → `syncOutboxPending`. `seed-dev.ts` clearTables list flippea `sync_queue` → `sync_outbox`. JSDoc cleanup atravesando `enqueue.ts` + `journal.ts` + `schema.ts` refleja el estado post-cutover. Counter Foundation Reset sube de 13/21 a 14/21. No quedan referencias server-side activas a `syncQueue` / `sync_queue`; los literales restantes son migraciones históricas, narrativa ADR, tests de migración/compatibilidad y el ObjectStore IndexedDB preservado del cliente. | Every writer routes through `enqueueSync`; `sync_queue` table is gone; `sync.*` procedures all read/write `sync_outbox`; web client file no longer collides on name. | **High** |

Decisiones de scope: (1) **CompanySyncCard dual-mount** — preservada en `/company?tab=data` para backward-compat; un follow-up `[ux] retire CompanySyncCard from /company once /operations is established` retira el duplicate cuando los operadores migren su workflow. (2) **Sin nuevas tablas / migrations** — toda la data ya existe en sync_outbox/fiscal_documents/hardware_outbox/site_peripherals. (3) **No fire-and-forget tick en retry** — operator-driven retry; el periodic worker (30s) drena la row requeued sin riesgo de re-fail inmediato cuando el error transient aún no resolvió. (4) **Reconciliation panels parqueados a ENG-065b** — Cash necesita `cashSessions.pendingChecks` enriquecido + nueva query de discrepancia (expected vs actual cash); Payment necesita un `payment_outbox` que aún no shippea (gated por ENG-063); Inventory necesita reconciliation queries entre `inventory_balances` y stock movements. (5) **Diagnostic Export parqueado a ENG-065c** — el operator pide JSON download para tickets de soporte; necesita server-side bundle endpoint + zipped client download flow. | Operator can see what is pending, what failed, and which action to take without reading logs. | **High** |
| `ENG-065b` | Operations Center: Cash + Inventory Reconciliation | Shipped | Second slice of ENG-065. Add Cash + Inventory reconciliation tabs to the existing `/operations` page using only tRPC procedures — no migrations, no new tables. Payment reconciliation explicitly carved out to `ENG-065d` (gated on ENG-063 `payment_outbox`). **Shipped**: dos procedures nuevas bajo `reports.*` (managerOrAdmin) — `reports.cash.reconciliation` (input `{limit?}`) corre tenant-wide drop del per-(siteId, cashier) filter del legacy `cashSessions.report`; agrega open sessions sin cutoff + closed sessions en ventana 30 días devolviendo `summary.{openSessionCount, closedRecentCount, reviewCount, netOverShort, largestDiscrepancy, windowDays}`, `bySite.[]` (per-site openSessions/closedSessions/netOverShort/overShortCount con epsilon `0.009`), y `recentDiscrepancies.[]` (top |overShort| closures, capped por limit) — y `reports.inventory.discrepancies` (input `{limit?}`) hace single GROUP BY contra `inventory_balances` + LEFT JOIN a products devolviendo `summary.{productsScanned, discrepancyCount, deltaEpsilon}` + `rows.[]` (productId/Name/Sku, cachedStock vs sumOfBalances, signed delta, siteCount) flag rows donde `|cachedStock - Σ(on_hand)| > 0.001`. La discrepancia es cache-vs-cache (`products.stock` vs `Σ(inventory_balances)`) que es exactamente la drift que `inventory.reconcileBalances` ya healing — NO es Σ-de-movements porque `inventory_movements` no tiene `site_id`. Decisiones de scope: (1) **Payment carved out a ENG-065d (gated)** — `payment_outbox` aún no existe y depende de ENG-063 (Payment terminal adapter). El operator no ve placeholder UI; el row gated abajo documenta la dependencia. (2) **Sin migraciones / tablas nuevas** — toda la data fue inferible del schema actual (cash_sessions + inventory_balances + products). | `ENG-065d` | Operations Center: Payment Reconciliation | Shipped | Third slice carved out from ENG-065b at planning time because the data layer dependency (`payment_outbox`) did not exist yet. ENG-038 slice 1 + ENG-038c provided the table, matcher, worker, and `suggestedAction` per mismatch. **Shipped 2026-05-14**: three new procedures on the existing `payments.*` router. `payments.retryOutbox({outboxId})` admin-only mutation flips a row back to `queued` with `attempts=0` / `nextRetryAt=null` / `claimToken=null` / `lockedAt=null` / `lastError=null`, refusing terminal `settled` rows with `PAYMENT_OUTBOX_NOT_RETRIABLE` so a confirmed settlement can never be silently undone via retry. `payments.markSettled({outboxId, providerTransactionId?})` admin-only mutation flips a row to `settled` with optional provider-tx override, idempotent on already-settled rows (no second audit row unless the operator supplied a new providerTransactionId that differs from the stored one). `payments.methodBreakdown({windowDays})` manager+admin read-only query aggregates `payment_outbox` by `(rail, status)` for the last N days (default 7, max 90) so the admin spots dead_letter pileups at a glance. Both mutations wrap the UPDATE + `writeAuditLog` in a single transaction with `before`/`after` snapshots; two new audit actions registered on both `auditLogActionEnum` server-side and the web mirror `AuditLogAction` union (`payment.retry`, `payment.mark_settled`) plus a `payment_outbox` resource type. | `ENG-066` | Backup, restore, and local security | Shipped | Threat-model local POS data; implement backup/restore expectations around outbox and device identity; decide key storage per OS; document no PAN/CVV storage and token/reference-only payment data. **Shipped 2026-05-07**: tres ejes de hardening + ADR-0006. (1) **Backup atómico**: nuevo `apps/desktop/src/main/backup/backup-bundle.ts` con `createBackupBundle()` que usa `better-sqlite3.backup()` (online backup API de SQLite) para snapshot atómico mientras el server corre, integrity-check via `PRAGMA integrity_check` post-snapshot, y bundle ZIP que viaja con `local.db` + `device-id.txt` + `manifest.json` (jszip nuevo dep en `apps/desktop`). (2) **Restore validado**: `extractBackupBundle()` detecta formato por magic bytes (ZIP `50 4b 03 04` vs SQLite `53 51 4c 69`), extrae a staging dir, corre `assertSqliteIntegrity()` ANTES del swap. Format-unrecognized + corruption → rechazo limpio sin tocar el live. ZIP bundles preservan device-id del backup; legacy `.db` bundles preservan destination identity. Backwards-compat con backups raw `.db` pre-ENG-066. (3) **Sanitization del diagnostic export** (ENG-065c hardening): `services/diagnostics/sanitize.ts::sanitizePayload()` walker recursivo con denylist anchored (`password`, `token`, `jwt`, `apiKey`, `clientSecret`, `pan`, `cvv`, `cardnumber`, `certificate`, `oauthtoken`, `authorizationcode` y ~25 más, ver `SENSITIVE_KEYS`). Manifest gana `sanitized: true` + `redactedKeysByTable` para auditabilidad del bundle. Matching anchored evita false-positives sobre keys benignas (`pancake_count`, `panel_layout`). Idempotente: re-aplicar sobre output ya saneado es no-op. (4) **Architectural lint anti-PAN/CVV**: nueva case en `__tests__/architectural-lint.test.ts` que escanea `db/schema.ts` por declaraciones `text(...)/integer(...)` con nombre matching `pan|cvv|cvc|card_number|cardholder_name|primary_account_number`. Bloquea cualquier futuro ticket que filtre una columna PAN al schema. (5) **ADR-0006** (`docs/architecture/0006-local-data-security.md`) documenta threat model + decisiones de scope: encryption-at-rest deferred, allowlist-vs-denylist tradeoff resuelto a denylist, per-OS keychain integration deferred a ENG-063 (`@node-gyp-build/keytar` candidate identificado), audit-log-on-restore deferred a ENG-066b. 15 server unit tests + 4 integration tests + 15 desktop `node --test` tests + 2 lint cases nuevos. ci:server / ci:web / ci:desktop verde. | `ENG-067b` | `hardware_outbox` envelope-keyed idempotency | Shipped | Cierra el gap estructural que la suite chaos de ENG-067 documentó: dos enqueues del mismo comando lógico (un retry tRPC tras un network blip, un replay desde el offline buffer, un worker reboot vía stale-claim sweep) producían DOS rows en `hardware_outbox` y el worker dispatchea ambos — el recibo se imprime dos veces o el cajón se patea dos veces. **Shipped 2026-05-06**: nueva migración `0018_hardware_outbox_idempotency.sql` agrega columna nullable `idempotency_key` + partial unique idx `(tenant_id, kind, idempotency_key) WHERE idempotency_key IS NOT NULL` (mirror del shape ENG-064 sync_outbox). Nuevo helper `services/peripherals/enqueue-hardware.ts::enqueueHardware(ctx, args)` que captura el `UNIQUE constraint failed.*hardware_outbox` y retorna `{id, deduped: true}` mirror estructural de `enqueueSync()`. Los 2 sitios inline en `routers/peripherals.ts` (fallback de `printReceipt` + de `kickCashDrawer`) cutover al helper. Input schemas extendidas con optional `idempotencyKey` + preprocess que acepta `''` como omitida — opt-in via input, NO upgrade a `criticalCommandProcedure` (las procedures siguen como `tenantProcedure`/`managerOrAdminProcedure`; el envelope-middleware path se promueve en un futuro ticket cuando el cliente UI envíe el header). Empty-string keys se normalizan a omitida en el schema publico y a null en el helper para no chocar con la partial idx. 8 cases nuevos en `enqueue-hardware.test.ts` (omit key → fresh row, first call con key → fresh, second con misma key → deduped same id, cross-tenant independencia, cross-kind independencia, empty-string normalize, FK violation rethrow no swallowed, public schema empty-string normalize). El chaos test `chaos-duplicate-retry.test.ts` flippeó: el subsuite "hardware_outbox has NO schema-level idempotency today" ahora se llama "hardware_outbox idempotent retry collapses to one row (ENG-067b)", la assertion pasó de `toHaveLength(2)` → `toHaveLength(1)` + `expect(r2.deduped).toBe(true)`, y el cross-tenant case usa `enqueueHardware` en lugar de `db.insert` directo. ADR-0003 footer agregó nota de paridad con sync_outbox idempotency. Counter Foundation Reset 18/21 → 19/21. Decisiones de scope: (1) **Sin upgrade a `criticalCommandProcedure`** — opt-in via input mantiene las procedures backward-compatible y la primitiva queda lista para que cualquier futuro caller (offline-print queue, ENG-066 backup/restore replay) opte. (2) **Sin web client wave** — el cliente UI no genera la idempotencyKey aún; el "user clicks twice → two prints" sigue siendo el comportamiento por default cuando no hay key. (3) **Empty-string normalize** evita un foot-gun: callers que pasan `''` desde un form vacío no rompen la dedup ni stackean rows. | Same-envelope retry to `hardware_outbox` collapses to one row; legacy null-key path stays independent. | **High** |

| `ENG-047` | AI anomaly follow-ups (sidebar badge + audit_logs persistence + snooze) | Shipped | Out-of-band ticket que cierra los tres `[ai]` follow-ups que el review de ENG-032 había capturado en BACKLOG. **(1) Sidebar badge** — el ítem `Dashboard` del nav muestra un contador rojo cuando hay alertas Alta pendientes. | `ENG-046` | CI minutes reduction — manual cross-OS desktop build | Shipped | Out-of-band ticket triggered by an operator pedido para reducir el consumo de minutos de GitHub Actions en cada push a main.
